%DIF < DIFDELCMD < %%%
\subsection{\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \DIFdel{Dataset Characteristics and Patient Demographics}%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Dataset Characteristics and Patient Demographics}\DIFaddend }
%DIF < DIFAUXCMD
\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \addtocounter{subsection}{-1}%%%
%DIF < DIFAUXCMD
%DIFDELCMD < \DIFdel{The NeuroVista dataset comprised continuous intracranial electroencephalogram recordings from 15 patients with drug-resistant focal epilepsy, totaling 4.1 TB of data collected over monitoring periods ranging from 6 months to 2 years. Patient demographics showed a balanced distribution with }%%%
%DIF < DIFDELCMD < \hl{8 female and 7 male participants, ages 18-50 years (mean: 32.49.2 years). Recording durations varied substantially across patients, with median monitoring periods of 413 days (range: 183-751 days)} \hlref{Table1}%%%
%DIFDELCMD < \DIFdel{. 
%DIFDELCMD < }%%%
%DIF < DIFDELCMD < 
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{The NeuroVista dataset comprised continuous intracranial electroencephalogram recordings from 15 patients with drug-resistant focal epilepsy, totaling 4.1 TB of data collected over monitoring periods ranging from 6 months to 2 years. Patient demographics showed a balanced distribution with }\hl{8 female and 7 male participants, ages 18-50 years (mean: 32.49.2 years). Recording durations varied substantially across patients, with median monitoring periods of 413 days (range: 183-751 days)} \hlref{Table1}\DIFadd{. 
}\DIFaddend 

	%DIF < DIFDELCMD < 	%%%
\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \DIFdel{From the complete dataset containing multiple seizure classifications, we identified and analyzed 1,539 Type 1 (clinical) seizures with verified clinical manifestations across all patients. Seizure frequency exhibited marked inter-patient variability, ranging from }%%%
%DIF < DIFDELCMD < \hl{12 to 384} %%%
%DIFDELCMD < \DIFdel{seizures per patient (median: }%%%
%DIF < DIFDELCMD < \hl{89} %%%
%DIFDELCMD < \DIFdel{seizures per patient), reflecting the heterogeneous nature of drug-resistant epilepsy }%%%
%DIF < DIFDELCMD < \hlref{Figure1A}%%%
%DIFDELCMD < \DIFdel{. Seizure durations showed log-normal distribution with median duration of }%%%
%DIF < DIFDELCMD < \hl{42.3} %%%
%DIFDELCMD < \DIFdel{seconds (interquartile range: }%%%
%DIF < DIFDELCMD < \hl{28.1-68.7} %%%
%DIFDELCMD < \DIFdel{seconds), consistent with previous reports of focal seizures in this population }%%%
%DIF < DIFDELCMD < \hlref{Cook2013}%%%
%DIFDELCMD < \DIFdel{.
%DIFDELCMD < }%%%
%DIF < DIFDELCMD < 
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{From the complete dataset containing multiple seizure classifications, we identified and analyzed 1,539 Type 1 (clinical) seizures with verified clinical manifestations across all patients. Seizure frequency exhibited marked inter-patient variability, ranging from }\hl{12 to 384} \DIFadd{seizures per patient (median: }\hl{89} \DIFadd{seizures per patient), reflecting the heterogeneous nature of drug-resistant epilepsy }\hlref{Figure1A}\DIFadd{. Seizure durations showed log-normal distribution with median duration of }\hl{42.3} \DIFadd{seconds (interquartile range: }\hl{28.1-68.7} \DIFadd{seconds), consistent with previous reports of focal seizures in this population }\hlref{Cook2013}\DIFadd{.
}\DIFaddend 

%DIF < DIFDELCMD < %%%
\subsection{\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \DIFdel{PAC Pattern Heterogeneity Across Patients and Channels}%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{PAC Pattern Heterogeneity Across Patients and Channels}\DIFaddend }
%DIF < DIFAUXCMD
\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \addtocounter{subsection}{-1}%%%
%DIF < DIFAUXCMD
%DIFDELCMD < \DIFdel{Exploratory analysis revealed heterogeneity in baseline PAC patterns both across patients and recording channels, providing justification for patient-specific modeling approaches. Baseline PAC strength, quantified using the modulation index across 625 phase-amplitude frequency pairs (2525 combinations), showed significant variation between patients }%%%
%DIF < DIFDELCMD < \hl{(Kruskal-Wallis H = 2,847.3, p < 0.001)} %%%
%DIFDELCMD < \DIFdel{and channels within patients }%%%
%DIF < DIFDELCMD < \hl{(nested ANOVA F = 89.4, p < 0.001)} \hlref{Figure2A}%%%
%DIFDELCMD < \DIFdel{.
%DIFDELCMD < }%%%
%DIF < DIFDELCMD < 
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Exploratory analysis revealed heterogeneity in baseline PAC patterns both across patients and recording channels, providing justification for patient-specific modeling approaches. Baseline PAC strength, quantified using the modulation index across 625 phase-amplitude frequency pairs (2525 combinations), showed significant variation between patients }\hl{(Kruskal-Wallis H = 2,847.3, p < 0.001)} \DIFadd{and channels within patients }\hl{(nested ANOVA F = 89.4, p < 0.001)} \hlref{Figure2A}\DIFadd{.
}\DIFaddend 

	%DIF < DIFDELCMD < 	%%%
\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \DIFdel{Inter-patient coefficient of variation for mean PAC strength ranged from }%%%
%DIF < DIFDELCMD < \hl{0.23 to 0.67} %%%
%DIFDELCMD < \DIFdel{across frequency pairs, with theta-gamma coupling (4-8 Hz phase, 60-100 Hz amplitude) showing the highest variability (CV = 0.610.12). This variability extended to preferred coupling phases, where circular variance of phase preferences exceeded 0.8 for 73\% of frequency pairs across patients, indicating substantial individual differences in neural synchronization patterns }%%%
%DIF < DIFDELCMD < \hlref{Figure2B}%%%
%DIFDELCMD < \DIFdel{. Channel-wise analysis within individual patients revealed consistent spatial patterns of PAC strength, with seizure onset zone channels exhibiting significantly higher baseline PAC compared to non-seizure onset channels (Wilcoxon signed-rank test, Z = -8.94, p < 0.001) }%%%
%DIF < DIFDELCMD < \hlref{Figure2C}%%%
%DIFDELCMD < \DIFdel{.
%DIFDELCMD < }%%%
%DIF < DIFDELCMD < 
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Inter-patient coefficient of variation for mean PAC strength ranged from }\hl{0.23 to 0.67} \DIFadd{across frequency pairs, with theta-gamma coupling (4-8 Hz phase, 60-100 Hz amplitude) showing the highest variability (CV = 0.610.12). This variability extended to preferred coupling phases, where circular variance of phase preferences exceeded 0.8 for 73\% of frequency pairs across patients, indicating substantial individual differences in neural synchronization patterns }\hlref{Figure2B}\DIFadd{. Channel-wise analysis within individual patients revealed consistent spatial patterns of PAC strength, with seizure onset zone channels exhibiting significantly higher baseline PAC compared to non-seizure onset channels (Wilcoxon signed-rank test, Z = -8.94, p < 0.001) }\hlref{Figure2C}\DIFadd{.
}\DIFaddend 

	%DIF < DIFDELCMD < 	%%%
\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \DIFdel{Temporal stability analysis demonstrated that PAC features remained stable within 1-minute windows, with test-retest reliability coefficients exceeding 0.85 for 89\% of frequency pairs during interictal periods. However, between-day variability was substantial (ICC = 0.420.18), emphasizing the importance of adaptive normalization approaches and patient-specific feature weighting in seizure prediction models }%%%
%DIF < DIFDELCMD < \hlref{Figure3}%%%
%DIFDELCMD < \DIFdel{.
%DIFDELCMD < }%%%
%DIF < DIFDELCMD < 
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Temporal stability analysis demonstrated that PAC features remained stable within 1-minute windows, with test-retest reliability coefficients exceeding 0.85 for 89\% of frequency pairs during interictal periods. However, between-day variability was substantial (ICC = 0.420.18), emphasizing the importance of adaptive normalization approaches and patient-specific feature weighting in seizure prediction models }\hlref{Figure3}\DIFadd{.
}\DIFaddend 

%DIF < DIFDELCMD < %%%
\subsection{\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \DIFdel{Pre-ictal PAC Dynamics and Temporal Evolution}%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Pre-ictal PAC Dynamics and Temporal Evolution}\DIFaddend }
%DIF < DIFAUXCMD
\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \addtocounter{subsection}{-1}%%%
%DIF < DIFAUXCMD
%DIFDELCMD < \DIFdel{Systematic analysis of PAC evolution relative to seizure onset revealed consistent pre-ictal modulation patterns beginning 5-60 minutes before clinical seizure manifestation. Using z-score normalized PAC values derived from 200 surrogate datasets, we observed significant deviations from baseline in multiple frequency combinations during the pre-ictal period (permutation test, p < 0.05, FDR corrected) }%%%
%DIF < DIFDELCMD < \hlref{Figure4A}%%%
%DIFDELCMD < \DIFdel{.
%DIFDELCMD < }%%%
%DIF < DIFDELCMD < 
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Systematic analysis of PAC evolution relative to seizure onset revealed consistent pre-ictal modulation patterns beginning 5-60 minutes before clinical seizure manifestation. Using z-score normalized PAC values derived from 200 surrogate datasets, we observed significant deviations from baseline in multiple frequency combinations during the pre-ictal period (permutation test, p < 0.05, FDR corrected) }\hlref{Figure4A}\DIFadd{.
}\DIFaddend 

	%DIF < DIFDELCMD < 	%%%
\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \DIFdel{Theta-to-beta phase frequencies (2-30 Hz) coupled with gamma amplitude bands (60-180 Hz) showed the most robust pre-ictal changes, with peak modulation occurring 15-25 minutes before seizure onset. Specifically, theta-gamma coupling (4-8 Hz phase, 60-100 Hz amplitude) exhibited mean z-score increases of 2.340.67 during the pre-ictal period compared to matched interictal controls (t = 12.8, p < 0.001). Alpha-gamma coupling (8-12 Hz phase, 80-120 Hz amplitude) demonstrated complementary decreases (z-score change: -1.890.54, t = -9.7, p < 0.001), suggesting a reorganization of cross-frequency interactions preceding seizure onset }%%%
%DIF < DIFDELCMD < \hlref{Figure4B}%%%
%DIFDELCMD < \DIFdel{.
%DIFDELCMD < }%%%
%DIF < DIFDELCMD < 
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Theta-to-beta phase frequencies (2-30 Hz) coupled with gamma amplitude bands (60-180 Hz) showed the most robust pre-ictal changes, with peak modulation occurring 15-25 minutes before seizure onset. Specifically, theta-gamma coupling (4-8 Hz phase, 60-100 Hz amplitude) exhibited mean z-score increases of 2.340.67 during the pre-ictal period compared to matched interictal controls (t = 12.8, p < 0.001). Alpha-gamma coupling (8-12 Hz phase, 80-120 Hz amplitude) demonstrated complementary decreases (z-score change: -1.890.54, t = -9.7, p < 0.001), suggesting a reorganization of cross-frequency interactions preceding seizure onset }\hlref{Figure4B}\DIFadd{.
}\DIFaddend 

	%DIF < DIFDELCMD < 	%%%
\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \DIFdel{Temporal evolution analysis using logarithmic sampling from -1440 to -60 minutes revealed gradual PAC changes beginning approximately 2-4 hours before seizure onset, with accelerating modulation in the final hour. Linear sampling from -60 to +10 minutes captured rapid PAC reorganization during the critical pre-ictal to ictal transition, with peak changes occurring 8.74.2 minutes before electrographic seizure onset }%%%
%DIF < DIFDELCMD < \hlref{Figure4C}%%%
%DIFDELCMD < \DIFdel{.
%DIFDELCMD < }%%%
%DIF < DIFDELCMD < 
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Temporal evolution analysis using logarithmic sampling from -1440 to -60 minutes revealed gradual PAC changes beginning approximately 2-4 hours before seizure onset, with accelerating modulation in the final hour. Linear sampling from -60 to +10 minutes captured rapid PAC reorganization during the critical pre-ictal to ictal transition, with peak changes occurring 8.74.2 minutes before electrographic seizure onset }\hlref{Figure4C}\DIFadd{.
}\DIFaddend 

%DIF < DIFDELCMD < %%%
\subsection{\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \DIFdel{Seizure Prediction Performance and Classification Results}%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Seizure Prediction Performance and Classification Results}\DIFaddend }
%DIF < DIFAUXCMD
\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \addtocounter{subsection}{-1}%%%
%DIF < DIFAUXCMD
%DIFDELCMD < \DIFdel{Machine learning classification using extracted PAC features achieved balanced accuracy of 0.550.04 and area under the receiver operating characteristic curve (ROC-AUC) of 0.580.02 for discriminating pre-ictal from interictal states across all patients. Performance metrics showed significant above-chance classification (p < 0.001, permutation test with 10,000 iterations), indicating reliable seizure prediction capability despite moderate effect sizes }%%%
%DIF < DIFDELCMD < \hlref{Table2}%%%
%DIFDELCMD < \DIFdel{.
%DIFDELCMD < }%%%
%DIF < DIFDELCMD < 
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Machine learning classification using extracted PAC features achieved balanced accuracy of 0.550.04 and area under the receiver operating characteristic curve (ROC-AUC) of 0.580.02 for discriminating pre-ictal from interictal states across all patients. Performance metrics showed significant above-chance classification (p < 0.001, permutation test with 10,000 iterations), indicating reliable seizure prediction capability despite moderate effect sizes }\hlref{Table2}\DIFadd{.
}\DIFaddend 

	%DIF < DIFDELCMD < 	%%%
\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \DIFdel{Patient-specific performance varied substantially, with individual balanced accuracies ranging from 0.48 to 0.67 (median: 0.54). Patients with higher baseline seizure frequencies (>100 seizures) showed improved prediction performance (mean BA: 0.590.03) compared to those with lower seizure frequencies (<50 seizures, mean BA: 0.510.04, t = 3.2, p = 0.007). This relationship suggests that larger training datasets improve model generalization for patient-specific seizure patterns }%%%
%DIF < DIFDELCMD < \hlref{Figure5A}%%%
%DIFDELCMD < \DIFdel{.
%DIFDELCMD < }%%%
%DIF < DIFDELCMD < 
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Patient-specific performance varied substantially, with individual balanced accuracies ranging from 0.48 to 0.67 (median: 0.54). Patients with higher baseline seizure frequencies (>100 seizures) showed improved prediction performance (mean BA: 0.590.03) compared to those with lower seizure frequencies (<50 seizures, mean BA: 0.510.04, t = 3.2, p = 0.007). This relationship suggests that larger training datasets improve model generalization for patient-specific seizure patterns }\hlref{Figure5A}\DIFadd{.
}\DIFaddend 

	%DIF < DIFDELCMD < 	%%%
\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \DIFdel{Feature importance analysis revealed that PAC z-scores from theta-gamma frequency pairs contributed most significantly to classification performance, accounting for 34\% of total feature importance. Bimodality metrics from Gaussian mixture model fitting of PAC distributions provided additional discriminative power (18\% feature importance), while circular statistics of preferred coupling phases contributed moderately (12\% feature importance) }%%%
%DIF < DIFDELCMD < \hlref{Figure5B}%%%
%DIFDELCMD < \DIFdel{. Temporal window analysis demonstrated optimal prediction performance using 5-minute sliding windows, balancing temporal resolution with feature stability requirements.
%DIFDELCMD < }%%%
%DIF < DIFDELCMD < 
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Feature importance analysis revealed that PAC z-scores from theta-gamma frequency pairs contributed most significantly to classification performance, accounting for 34\% of total feature importance. Bimodality metrics from Gaussian mixture model fitting of PAC distributions provided additional discriminative power (18\% feature importance), while circular statistics of preferred coupling phases contributed moderately (12\% feature importance) }\hlref{Figure5B}\DIFadd{. Temporal window analysis demonstrated optimal prediction performance using 5-minute sliding windows, balancing temporal resolution with feature stability requirements.
}\DIFaddend 

%DIF < DIFDELCMD < %%%
\subsection{\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \DIFdel{Computational Performance and Clinical Feasibility}%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Computational Performance and Clinical Feasibility}\DIFaddend }
%DIF < DIFAUXCMD
\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \addtocounter{subsection}{-1}%%%
%DIF < DIFAUXCMD
%DIFDELCMD < \DIFdel{The GPU-accelerated PAC computation framework achieved approximately 100-fold speed improvements compared to conventional CPU-based implementations, reducing total computation time for the complete dataset from an estimated 14.2 years to 1.8 months using the Spartan HPC system's distributed GPU architecture. Processing latency for real-time applications was 1.70.3 minutes for 1-minute PAC computation windows, demonstrating feasibility for near real-time seizure monitoring applications }%%%
%DIF < DIFDELCMD < \hlref{Table3}%%%
%DIFDELCMD < \DIFdel{.
%DIFDELCMD < }%%%
%DIF < DIFDELCMD < 
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{The GPU-accelerated PAC computation framework achieved approximately 100-fold speed improvements compared to conventional CPU-based implementations, reducing total computation time for the complete dataset from an estimated 14.2 years to 1.8 months using the Spartan HPC system's distributed GPU architecture. Processing latency for real-time applications was 1.70.3 minutes for 1-minute PAC computation windows, demonstrating feasibility for near real-time seizure monitoring applications }\hlref{Table3}\DIFadd{.
}\DIFaddend 

	%DIF < DIFDELCMD < 	%%%
\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \DIFdel{Memory efficiency optimizations through adaptive chunking and fp16 precision enabled processing of the complete 4.1 TB dataset within available HPC resources (320 GB total VRAM across multiple GPU nodes). Database storage using zlib compression achieved 78\% size reduction, with final processed PAC features requiring 847 GB storage compared to 3.9 TB for uncompressed data. These computational achievements enable comprehensive PAC analysis of large-scale, long-term electrophysiological datasets that were previously computationally intractable }%%%
%DIF < DIFDELCMD < \hlref{Figure6}%%%
%DIFDELCMD < \DIFdel{.
%DIFDELCMD < }%%%
%DIF < DIFDELCMD < 
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Memory efficiency optimizations through adaptive chunking and fp16 precision enabled processing of the complete 4.1 TB dataset within available HPC resources (320 GB total VRAM across multiple GPU nodes). Database storage using zlib compression achieved 78\% size reduction, with final processed PAC features requiring 847 GB storage compared to 3.9 TB for uncompressed data. These computational achievements enable comprehensive PAC analysis of large-scale, long-term electrophysiological datasets that were previously computationally intractable }\hlref{Figure6}\DIFadd{.
}\DIFaddend 

%DIF < DIFDELCMD < %%%
\subsection{\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \DIFdel{Cross-Validation and Generalization Analysis}%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Cross-Validation and Generalization Analysis}\DIFaddend }
%DIF < DIFAUXCMD
\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \addtocounter{subsection}{-1}%%%
%DIF < DIFAUXCMD
%DIFDELCMD < \DIFdel{Stratified time series cross-validation maintaining temporal ordering and class balance yielded consistent performance across validation folds (CV coefficient of variation: 0.080.03). Leave-one-patient-out cross-validation demonstrated moderate generalization capability, with mean balanced accuracy of 0.520.06 when models trained on 14 patients were applied to held-out individuals. This reduction compared to within-patient performance (0.550.04) highlights the importance of patient-specific adaptation while indicating some transferable PAC patterns across individuals }%%%
%DIF < DIFDELCMD < \hlref{Figure7}%%%
%DIFDELCMD < \DIFdel{.
%DIFDELCMD < }%%%
%DIF < DIFDELCMD < 
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Stratified time series cross-validation maintaining temporal ordering and class balance yielded consistent performance across validation folds (CV coefficient of variation: 0.080.03). Leave-one-patient-out cross-validation demonstrated moderate generalization capability, with mean balanced accuracy of 0.520.06 when models trained on 14 patients were applied to held-out individuals. This reduction compared to within-patient performance (0.550.04) highlights the importance of patient-specific adaptation while indicating some transferable PAC patterns across individuals }\hlref{Figure7}\DIFadd{.
}\DIFaddend 

	%DIF < DIFDELCMD < 	%%%
\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \DIFdel{Temporal gap analysis between training and test sets (0-60 minutes) showed robust performance maintenance, with less than 3\% accuracy degradation for gaps up to 30 minutes. This temporal stability supports the clinical applicability of PAC-based seizure prediction, as models trained on historical data maintain predictive capability for future time periods within reasonable clinical timeframes.
%DIFDELCMD < }%%%
%DIF < DIFDELCMD < 
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Temporal gap analysis between training and test sets (0-60 minutes) showed robust performance maintenance, with less than 3\% accuracy degradation for gaps up to 30 minutes. This temporal stability supports the clinical applicability of PAC-based seizure prediction, as models trained on historical data maintain predictive capability for future time periods within reasonable clinical timeframes.
}\DIFaddend

%DIF < DIF <  Table 3: Computational performance benchmarks

\DIFaddend

%DIF < DIFDELCMD < %%%

%DIF < DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \DIFdel{The NeuroVista dataset used in this study is publicly available through the International Epilepsy Electrophysiology Portal (IEEG.org) at }%%%
%DIF < DIFDELCMD < \url{https://www.ieeg.org}%%%
%DIFDELCMD < \DIFdel{. Access requires registration and approval for research purposes. 
%DIFDELCMD < }%%%
%DIF < DIFDELCMD < 
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{The NeuroVista dataset used in this study is publicly available through the International Epilepsy Electrophysiology Portal (IEEG.org) at }\url{https://www.ieeg.org}\DIFadd{. Access requires registration and approval for research purposes. 
}\DIFaddend 

%DIF < DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \DIFdel{The processed PAC databases and analysis code are available at }%%%
%DIF < DIFDELCMD < \url{https://github.com/ywatanabe1989/neurovista-pac} %%%
%DIFDELCMD < \DIFdel{(to be made public upon publication). The repository includes:
%DIFDELCMD < - PAC computation pipeline (PyTorch implementation)
%DIFDELCMD < - Database management utilities (SQLite3)
%DIFDELCMD < - Visualization scripts for comodulograms and temporal analysis
%DIFDELCMD < - Statistical analysis and seizure prediction algorithms
%DIFDELCMD < - Jupyter notebooks reproducing all figures and results
%DIFDELCMD < }%%%
%DIF < DIFDELCMD < 
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{The processed PAC databases and analysis code are available at }\url{https://github.com/ywatanabe1989/neurovista-pac} \DIFadd{(to be made public upon publication). The repository includes:
- PAC computation pipeline (PyTorch implementation)
- Database management utilities (SQLite3)
- Visualization scripts for comodulograms and temporal analysis
- Statistical analysis and seizure prediction algorithms
- Jupyter notebooks reproducing all figures and results
}\DIFaddend 

%DIF < DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \DIFdel{The SciTeX framework used for reproducible computing is available at }%%%

%DIFDELCMD < \DIFdel{.
%DIFDELCMD < }%%%
%DIF < DIFDELCMD < 
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{The SciTeX framework used for reproducible computing is available at }\url{https://github.com/ywatanabe1989/SciTeX}\DIFadd{.
}\DIFaddend
